\begin{document}
\title{On the Provenance of a Pre-Complex Body: A Finite Real Response-Algebra Core}
\author{Jan Seeck\\Independent researcher\\\texttt{jan.seeck1@gmail.com}}
\date{Finite code snapshot: July 10, 2026\\Documentation revision: July 17, 2026}
\maketitle
\begin{abstract}
This article presents the discrete--finite core of the ComplemeNt Net Architecture (CNNA), initialized by an empty configuration and generated by an explicit deterministic rule family. The rooted carrier is not introduced as a discretization of a pre-existing space or spacetime, but as a finite, deterministic, and exactly inspectable substrate for genealogical provenance and boundary reduction. The structural index \(b\), depth cutoff \(L\), mode \(m\), and update schedule \(\mathfrak{s}\) are distinct; reference calculations fix \(m\) and \(\mathfrak{s}\) by stated commands rather than deriving them from the empty configuration. The term complement has a precise birth-relative meaning: an accepted birth enlarges the finite vertex carrier by a disjoint singleton coordinate, while a causal-layer update enlarges it by the direct sum of all newborn coordinates in that layer. These new carrier directions are then coupled to the existing network by directed parent--child, ancestor, and sibling weights. The implementation produces finite histories, terminal carriers, directed live and record edge layers, and a symmetrized control, without continuum fields, integrals, differential operators, or limits. For fixed inputs it computes carrier states, projectivity and orientation diagnostics, Schur-complement responses, symmetric/skew decompositions, finite \(J\)-objects, finite algebra and GNS quotients, local operator checks, sign transport, and live--record backreaction observables. Every reported object is a finite array, edge dictionary, matrix, residual, or generated row.

Dirichlet-to-Neumann terminology refers only to finite weighted networks: the maps are explicit Schur complements with declared boundary/interior partitions and residuals. No analytic boundary calculus is assumed. The calculations distinguish directed live and record structures from the symmetrized control and expose satisfied and failed finite properties. The relation to recent growing-tree models, finite-network effective operators, and tree Dirichlet-to-Neumann constructions is stated by explicit model-separation criteria rather than by a literature-wide novelty claim.

The result is not an infinite or continuum theory. It includes an exact, linearly growing real carrier system with non-unital corner embeddings, while independently reconstructed response, state, GNS, and finite-\(J\) objects retain quantified interlevel drift. Infinite completions, convergence claims, and continuum comparisons remain separate problems.
\end{abstract}
\newpage
\tableofcontents
\newpage

\section{Methodological position and scope}\label{sec:methodological-position}
The present construction is not introduced as a finite-dimensional approximation of an already specified quantum theory. Its question is logically prior: which response-theoretic and algebraic structures can be constructed before a complex Hilbert space, a complex observable algebra, a Hamiltonian, or a continuum geometry is assumed? The dependency order investigated here is
\begin{equation}
\begin{gathered}
  \emptyset
  \longrightarrow
  \text{finite }b\text{-ary address growth}
  \longrightarrow
  \text{birth-relative real carrier complements},\\
  \text{carrier complements}
  \longrightarrow
  \text{directed record/live weights}
  \longrightarrow
  \text{finite Schur boundary response},\\
  \Lambda^{\rm dir}
  \longrightarrow
  S=\tfrac12\bigl(\Lambda^{\rm dir}+(\Lambda^{\rm dir})^T\bigr),\\
  \Lambda^{\rm dir}
  \longrightarrow
  A=\tfrac12\bigl(\Lambda^{\rm dir}-(\Lambda^{\rm dir})^T\bigr),\\
  (S,A)
  \longrightarrow
  \text{finite real algebra}
  \longrightarrow
  \text{positive state},\\
  \text{positive state}
  \longrightarrow
  \text{real GNS quotient}
  \longrightarrow
  \text{finite complex-structure candidate}.
\end{gathered}
\label{eq:finite-provenance-chain}
\end{equation}
Here complement is not a metaphor and not a claim about an operator-algebraic commutant. At a birth event it is first the exact set-theoretic and coordinate-linear decomposition of the post-birth carrier into the pre-birth carrier and the newborn coordinate. The directed weights subsequently couple that new direction to the prior network. The skew sector is therefore not supplied by the word complement itself: it can occur only because the coupling rule is directed and because the resulting asymmetry survives the selected Schur reduction. Section~\ref{sec:birth-relative-complement} states these distinctions formally.

\paragraph{Substrate-selection criterion.}
The carrier choice follows a non-circularity requirement. If continuum geometry, spacetime, the causal and metric structure of spacetime, or complex-linear kinematics are among the structures whose provenance is under investigation, they cannot simultaneously be inserted as primitive input. The finite core therefore starts with neither a manifold, metric, measure, continuum field, differential operator, nor stochastic growth law. It requires instead a deterministic carrier that is finite at every stage, exposes every accepted growth event, has exact genealogical addresses, supports nontrivial branching, and admits explicit finite boundary elimination.

Subject to these requirements, rooted $b$-ary trees with $b\geq 2$ are among the simplest sufficiently rich carriers. A path carrier is combinatorially simpler but has no sibling branching, whereas an arbitrary graph would add adjacency choices that are not yet derived at the initial stage. The selection is therefore a methodological minimality statement under the stated requirements, not a uniqueness theorem and not a claim that every alternative discrete substrate has been excluded.

Earlier work with post-critically finite Sierpi\'nski-type complexes informed this selection because their finite graph approximants and finite boundary sets support a rigorous theory of compatible resistance and Dirichlet forms, Laplacians, and spectral analysis~\cite{Kigami1993,Kigami2001,Strichartz2006}. That setting supplied a controlled example of hierarchical response theory without requiring a smooth manifold as the starting object and motivated the move to an explicit branching provenance carrier. In the present finite CNNA derivation, however, no Sierpi\'nski gasket or tetrahedron, Euclidean embedding, self-similar continuum set, resistance-form limit, or fractal Laplacian is an input. The rooted tree is the primitive provenance carrier. Any later relation between that tree and a Sierpi\'nski-type complex is a separate gluing or duality problem and must be constructed and checked independently.
This order differs from frameworks in which a complex operator algebra, a quantum state space, or prescribed finite-dimensional algebraic connecting data belong to the initial specification. For example, algebraic quantum field theory starts from local observable algebras and their structural relations~\cite{HaagKastler1964}; AF constructions start from finite-dimensional $C^*$-algebras together with embedding data~\cite{Bratteli1972}; and finitely correlated spin-chain states start from a finite-dimensional auxiliary algebra and a positive map~\cite{FannesNachtergaeleWerner1992}. These comparisons locate the logical starting point of the present work; they do not assert equivalence with those theories.

A closer methodological comparator is the construction of complex structures on real jet spaces by Finster and Kamran~\cite{FinsterKamran2021}. In the setting of causal variational principles, conserved surface-layer forms are used to define an almost-complex structure, and additional conditions are analyzed under which it gives a canonical complex structure that combines with a scalar product to form a complex Hilbert space and subsequently supports bosonic Fock-space dynamics. The present article neither adopts a causal variational principle nor starts from jet spaces or surface-layer forms. It begins instead with finite real network growth and boundary response and asks whether a skew-response sector, a real algebra, a state, a real GNS quotient, and a finite $J$-candidate can be obtained along that explicit dependency chain. Consequently, unresolved sign and interlevel-naturality defects are retained as finite obstructions rather than removed by assuming the additional conditions required for a canonical complex structure. The relation between the two approaches is therefore a shared provenance question, not an identity of primitives, constructions, or results.

The distinction does not lie in the individual mathematical tools. Schur complements, finite network response maps, finite matrix algebras, positive functionals, and GNS constructions are established structures. The specific object investigated here is their connection by an explicit finite provenance chain whose interfaces are audited for hidden dependencies. The tree is therefore not interpreted directly as physical space, spacetime, or an observable algebra. It first records genealogical provenance. Each accepted address adds an exactly identifiable carrier direction complementary to the carrier already present at that update; the network character begins when this direction is coupled by the generated directed weights. Candidate observable structure appears only after this complement-coupling step, live--record separation, boundary reduction, and algebra generation.

In particular, the complex unit is not inserted through the scalar field of the initial construction. A real skew-response sector is constructed first, and only then is a finite operator $J$ tested for the algebraic relation associated with a complex structure. The residual transformation $J\mapsto-J$ is retained as an obstruction whenever the available real data do not distinguish the two orientations. Thus a successful finite $J$ test is not itself an absolute orientation theorem.

The finite restriction is deliberate. Every node, edge, response matrix, algebra generator, state, quotient operation, and residual remains explicitly inspectable. No continuum limit, von Neumann closure, modular flow, or type classification is used to justify an earlier stage of the construction. The results should therefore be read as a finite structure theory: they determine what can already be constructed or excluded at finite depth and identify the additional compatibility conditions required for an infinite operator-algebraic handoff.

The novelty claim is correspondingly limited. The article does not claim that its constituent techniques are individually new, that no related provenance-oriented construction exists, or that the finite core already defines a quantum field theory, an inductive-limit $C^*$-algebra, or a continuum spacetime model. It claims a specific auditable architecture and the finite results proved or computed within that architecture.

\paragraph{Development note.} The line of inquiry leading to the present finite core has evolved through more than four years of independent study, implementation, rejected constructions, falsification, and progressive scope reduction. Parts of this development are preserved in public, time-stamped records beginning in late 2021, including contemporaneous forum discussions; some intervening material is no longer completely recoverable. These records document the continuity and changing scope of the inquiry, not the prior existence of CNNA in its present form. Earlier exploratory formulations considered broader deterministic, fractal, network, open-system, and operator-algebraic interpretations. They are not used as premises or evidence in this article. The present work deliberately retains only the finite definitions, source-level constructions, generated results, and explicit obstructions reproducible from the supplied package. The documented history establishes the provenance of the inquiry, not the validity of its mathematical claims, which stand or fall on the construction and checks presented here.


\section{Recent related work and model separation}\label{sec:related-work}
The phrase \emph{growing tree} covers several mathematically distinct constructions. In one class the finite combinatorial carrier itself changes by the addition, deletion, or rearrangement of vertices and edges. In another class a random subtree, occupied cluster, or labeling grows inside a maximal or already specified carrier. A third class keeps the graph fixed and constructs or reconstructs a boundary-response operator on that graph. These distinctions matter here because the present finite core combines carrier growth, an immutable birth record, later updates of a separate live layer, directed real couplings, and a forward Schur boundary reduction. No single shared noun such as ``tree'', ``growth'', or ``Dirichlet-to-Neumann map'' is sufficient to identify the constructions.

\subsection{Comparison criteria}
The comparisons below use the following explicit questions.
\begin{enumerate}
\item What is primitive input: a maximal tree, a finite tree, a metric or quantum graph, or only a root and a branching bound?
\item What actually grows: the carrier, a selected subtree or occupation pattern, a labeling, or only an associated response matrix?
\item Is the evolution deterministic or stochastic, and is its ordering sequential, generation-wise, or synchronous on an active frontier?
\item Are previously accepted vertices and genealogical addresses preserved, or can the earlier tree be rearranged during a growth step?
\item Is there a birth-relative immutable record distinct from a state that is updated by later births?
\item Is a boundary response constructed, and if so, is it a forward finite Schur response or an inverse reconstruction problem?
\end{enumerate}
These criteria are descriptive. They locate the finite CNNA core among adjacent models without asserting that the cited sample exhausts the literature on random trees, branching processes, graph growth, or inverse problems.

\subsection{Recent tree-growth models}
Marckert constructs a sequence of uniformly distributed rooted $d$-ary trees in which the passage from size $n-1$ to size $n$ adds a node and rearranges part of the previous tree~\cite{Marckert2023}. This is a genuine carrier-growth construction and therefore a close combinatorial comparator. Its purpose is uniform random generation, however, and the rearrangement step means that the earlier finite tree is not retained as an immutable genealogical record in the sense used here.

Fredes and Marckert study and survey models of random subtrees of a connected graph, including uniform sampling of an $n$-vertex subtree of a specified ambient graph~\cite{FredesMarckert2023}. This cleanly illustrates the second meaning of growth used above: the selected subtree changes while the ambient carrier is already present. The present finite core instead treats accepted births as enlargements of the carrier itself; it does not sample an occupied subtree of a pre-existing graph.

Dunlop and Mardin study bounded-generation Bienaym\'e--Galton--Watson trees with nearest-neighbor ancestor interaction~\cite{DunlopMardin2022}. A random configuration is represented as a rooted subtree of a specified maximal tree, and the offspring variables and coupling determine the probability law. Thus the maximal carrier and stochastic law are primitive, whereas the present construction uses a deterministic accepted-birth sequence on the finite carrier and separates the frozen birth record from the subsequently updated live response.

Bodini, Genitrini, Mailler, and Naima study increasing and strict monotonic Schr\"oder trees generated by evolutionary rules in which labels encode the chronological order of branching events~\cite{BodiniGenitriniMaillerNaima2022}. Their first model selects one leaf at each step, while the strict monotonic model can select several leaves carrying the same chronological label. These are direct comparators for sequential versus synchronized event order. Their chronology is explicit in the labeling rule and supports random-tree enumeration and sampling; it is not a split between an immutable edge record and a later-updated network response.

Bodini, Genitrini, and Nurligareev introduce growing binary trees with internal nodes, active leaves, and dead leaves~\cite{BodiniGenitriniNurligareev2026}. Starting from one active leaf at $t=0$, every active leaf is synchronously replaced at each positive integer time either by a dead leaf or by an internal binary branch. This provides a particularly direct comparator for the \code{layer\_batch} control schedule: both organize a whole active frontier by discrete layers. The cited model adds an extinction rule and develops enumerative and sampling results; it does not construct birth-relative record/live edge layers or a network response that feeds back on previously born vertices.

\subsection{Recent boundary-response constructions on trees and finite networks}
Gernandt and Rohleder recover a finite weighted tree and its positive edge weights from the Dirichlet-to-Neumann matrix of its graph Laplacian~\cite{GernandtRohleder2022}. The tree and symmetric weighted Laplacian belong to a fixed inverse problem, and the boundary matrix is used to reconstruct weighted distances and hence the tree. The present direction is forward rather than inverse: the finite carrier and directed record/live weights are generated first, after which a selected boundary/interior partition is Schur-reduced.

Beard, Stefan, Viator, and Welters formulate effective operators for discrete electrical network problems by block-operator and Schur-complement methods and relate the finite-network effective operator to a discrete Dirichlet-to-Neumann map~\cite{BeardStefanViatorWelters2023}. This supplies a recent operator-theoretic comparator for finite elimination and variational response. Their graph and constitutive operator are fixed problem data; carrier growth, immutable birth provenance, and a directed record/live split are not part of that construction.

Peng and Song develop sparsified block elimination for Eulerian directed Laplacians, with augmented matrices whose Schur complements encode elimination errors~\cite{PengSong2022}. This confirms that Schur-based elimination has a substantial modern theory beyond symmetric graph Laplacians. The aim there is an approximate linear-system solver on a fixed directed Laplacian class; it is not an exact forward boundary response generated from a birth history, and it has no record/live distinction.

Avdonin, Khmelnytskaya, and Kravchenko give a progressive synthesis of the Weyl matrix, equivalently the transposed Dirichlet-to-Neumann map, of a quantum tree by successively attaching edges and computing the larger response from smaller ones~\cite{AvdoninKhmelnytskayaKravchenko2023}. This is especially relevant because both the tree and its boundary matrix are enlarged step by step. The quantum-tree setting nevertheless starts from metric edges, Sturm--Liouville equations, potentials, matching conditions, and a spectral parameter. The finite CNNA core starts instead from a real combinatorial carrier and directed finite weights and uses no differential equation or metric-edge input.

\begin{longtable}{>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.145\linewidth}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.205\linewidth}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.145\linewidth}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.185\linewidth}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.235\linewidth}}

\toprule
\textbf{Comparator} & \textbf{Primitive carrier and actual growth} & \textbf{Order or randomness} & \textbf{Provenance and response} & \textbf{Exact separation from the present core}\\
\midrule
\endfirsthead
\toprule
\textbf{Comparator} & \textbf{Primitive carrier and actual growth} & \textbf{Order or randomness} & \textbf{Provenance and response} & \textbf{Exact separation from the present core}\\
\midrule
\endhead
Marckert~\cite{Marckert2023} & Rooted $d$-ary carrier grows by one node, with rearrangement of prior structure. & Random construction with uniform size-$n$ marginal. & No record/live response split; no Schur--DtN layer. & Close carrier-growth comparator, but previous genealogy may be rearranged and the objective is uniform random generation.\\
\hline
Fredes--Marckert~\cite{FredesMarckert2023} & Selected subtree of a fixed connected ambient graph. & Markov-chain and random sampling models. & Subtree statistics; no carrier-birth record or forward DtN response. & The occupation/subtree grows inside a pre-existing carrier; CNNA enlarges the finite carrier itself.\\
\hline
Dunlop--Mardin~\cite{DunlopMardin2022} & Random rooted subtree of a specified maximal bounded tree. & Stochastic offspring law with generation bound and interaction. & Configuration statistics and recursion; no immutable birth record or forward DtN response. & The maximal carrier and probability law are inputs; CNNA grows the accepted finite carrier deterministically.\\
\hline
Bodini--Genitrini--Mailler--Naima~\cite{BodiniGenitriniMaillerNaima2022} & Labelled Schr\"oder carrier generated by replacing selected leaves. & Sequential one-leaf or synchronized multi-leaf chronological labels; random-tree analysis. & Labels record event chronology; no record/live response split or Schur--DtN layer. & Close event-order comparator, but chronology is an explicit label rule rather than a later network response.\\
\hline
Bodini--Genitrini--Nurligareev~\cite{BodiniGenitriniNurligareev2026} & Binary active frontier grows or becomes extinct. & External integer time; synchronous update of every active leaf. & Enumerative profile and sampler; no record/live response split. & Direct comparator for \code{layer\_batch}, not for the sequential schedule or later directed backreaction.\\
\hline
Gernandt--Rohleder~\cite{GernandtRohleder2022} & Fixed finite weighted tree. & No growth dynamics. & Symmetric Laplacian DtN matrix used for inverse reconstruction. & Inverse fixed-tree problem with positive symmetric weights, rather than generated directed forward response.\\
\hline
Beard--Stefan--Viator--Welters~\cite{BeardStefanViatorWelters2023} & Fixed finite network and constitutive operator. & No carrier growth. & Effective operator and DtN map obtained by Schur methods. & Strong response-theoretic comparator, but no genealogical carrier growth or record/live layering.\\
\hline
Peng--Song~\cite{PengSong2022} & Fixed Eulerian directed Laplacian system. & Algorithmic block elimination and sparsification. & Directed Schur complements encode elimination errors; no birth provenance. & Relevant to directed elimination, but approximate solver theory rather than exact generated boundary response.\\
\hline
Avdonin--Khmelnytskaya--Kravchenko~\cite{AvdoninKhmelnytskayaKravchenko2023} & Metric quantum tree enlarged by attaching edges. & Successive constructive synthesis. & Weyl/DtN matrix of larger tree computed from smaller matrices. & Progressive response growth is close, but metric edges, differential equations, and spectral data are primitive.\\
\hline
Present finite CNNA core & Root plus branching bound; accepted births enlarge the finite real carrier. & Deterministic selector $\mathfrak{s}$; sequential reference mode and synchronous comparison mode. & Immutable record layer, later-updated live layer, directed weights, and forward finite Schur response. & The combined object studied here; stronger infinite, continuum, uniqueness, and literature-wide novelty claims are not made.\\
\bottomrule
\end{longtable}

\subsection{Claim boundary}
The cited works show that node-by-node $d$-ary growth, random subtrees of fixed graphs, interacting branching subtrees, chronology-labelled increasing trees, synchronous binary-front evolution, finite Schur effective operators, directed-Laplacian block elimination, inverse tree DtN reconstruction, and progressive quantum-tree Weyl synthesis are established but distinct constructions. The present claim is correspondingly narrow: the inspected finite source realizes a specific deterministic combination of carrier growth, birth-relative coordinate extension, immutable record data, later live updates, directed coupling, and forward Schur reduction. This section does not prove that no mathematically equivalent formulation exists elsewhere, and it does not use the publication date of a reference as evidence for or against the validity of a mathematical statement.

\paragraph{Revision note.}
This documentation revision expands the recent-literature comparison and completes DOI or persistent-link metadata in the reference list. It changes neither the finite construction, the Python source, the generated row files, the reported numerical values, nor the finite claim boundary of the July 10 code snapshot.

\section{Source surface and execution basis}
\subsection{Inspected source tree}
The inspected source surface is supplied as arXiv ancillary material in \src{anc/CNNA_structured_core_pkg}. All package paths stated below are relative to that ancillary package root. The reproducible source-surface digest is computed over the Python files in the declared source boundary and excludes the article source, environment records, license, package checks, and other ancillary metadata:
\[
\code{2612012d5149bedca71dbdbe60d0cbd075bbda6171ca008e989482787a002044}.
\]
The digest is the SHA256 value of the line-sorted manifest stored in \src{docs/SOURCE_SURFACE_MANIFEST.txt}. Per-file checksums for the complete ancillary package are stored separately in \src{CHECKSUMS.txt}. The byte hash of the outer transport ZIP is not used as the mathematical source identity, because an archive may be unpacked or repackaged without changing the declared source files.

The source boundary for this document is the Python source surface
\[
\begin{gathered}
\code{src/cnna/\_\_init\_\_.py},\quad
\code{src/cnna/config.py},\quad
\code{src/cnna/io},\\
\code{src/cnna/core},\quad
\code{src/cnna/derived\_\allowbreak{}quantities},\quad
\code{src/cnna/object\_\allowbreak{}checks},\\
\code{src/cnna/analysis\_\allowbreak{}entrypoints},\quad
\code{run\_*.py}\text{ at package root.}
\end{gathered}
\]
The \code{config.py} file supplies numerical constants and reference selectors used by row construction. The \code{io} subtree supplies row-file writers and JSON hashing. The \code{object\_\allowbreak{}checks} subtree is part of the documented source surface where the local-support, Tomita, commutant, split, entropy, and refined-basis row families are generated by their stated commands. Existing files ending in \code{.md} or \code{.csv} are not used as mathematical source text. Result files produced before the current growth rule are outside the evidential surface of this document. CSV files may be named later only as outputs generated from the current package by a stated command.

\end{longtable}

\subsection{Minimal finite data route}
The executable route from a finite input tuple to row files is:
\[
\begin{array}{c}
(b,L,m,\mathfrak{s})
\longrightarrow \mathcal G_{b,L,m,\mathfrak{s}}
\longrightarrow (E^{\rm live},E^{\rm record},E^{\rm sym})\\[0.25em]
\longrightarrow \Lambda_B
\longrightarrow M_B=S_B+A_B
\longrightarrow (J_B^{\rm fin},\mathcal A_R,\mathcal H_R^{\rm GNS})\\[0.25em]
\longrightarrow \text{local row surfaces and live-record row surfaces}.
\end{array}
\]
For a fixed command, the row files are finite evaluations of this route. The local-operator command uses the same growth-schedule argument as the integrated command.

\subsection{Row status fields}
The row files contain text fields that record finite branch outcomes. The following strings occur as data values in the current row surface.
\begin{longtable}{>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.24\linewidth}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.68\linewidth}}
\caption{Status strings and finite branch meanings.}\label{tab:status-strings}\\
\toprule
\textbf{Status field value} & \textbf{Finite branch meaning}\\
\midrule
\endfirsthead
\toprule
\textbf{Status field value} & \textbf{Finite branch meaning}\\
\midrule
\endhead
\code{finite\_object} & the row contains the finite matrix/vector/scalar object for the selected input tuple.\\
\hline
\code{unavailable\_rank\_below\_2} & the support used for the finite two-plane object has rank below two, so the two-plane object is not returned.\\
\hline
\code{not\_residual\_le\_tolerance} & the row exists and its residual is greater than the tolerance field carried by the row.\\
\hline
\code{coarse\_frontier} & the row uses a coarse frontier region selected by the directed-frontier cap.\\
\hline
\code{law\_fit\_eligible=0} & the row is present but excluded from the birth-relative fit route by its row fields.\\
\hline
\code{law\_fit\_eligible=1} & the row is present in the birth-relative fit route.\\
\bottomrule
\end{longtable}


\subsection{Integrated execution command}
The integrated root entrypoint for the source surface documented here is \code{run\_cnna.py}. It dispatches to \code{cnna.analysis\_\allowbreak{}entrypoints.run\_\allowbreak{}cnna\_\allowbreak{}analysis.main} and invokes the row functions exported by \code{cnna.derived\_\allowbreak{}quantities}. The following command generates the row families for the integrated row surface:
\begin{verbatim}
cd anc/CNNA_structured_core_pkg
PYTHONPATH=src python3 run_cnna.py \
  --branching 3 \
  --levels 4 5 6 \
  --modes linear log saturating \
  --states live record sym \
  --max-regions 1 \
  --max-boundary 600 \
  --max-interior 900 \
  --directed-frontier-cap 6 \
  --algebra-tol 1e-10 \
  --algebra-max-iter 8 \
  --gns-tol 1e-10 \
  --growth-schedule layer_batch \
  --outdir outputs/core_derived_documentation_run
\end{verbatim}
A smaller finite run with the same entrypoint generates a reduced row surface for layout and source-route checks:
\begin{verbatim}
cd anc/CNNA_structured_core_pkg
PYTHONPATH=src python3 run_cnna.py \
  --branching 3 \
  --levels 4 5 \
  --modes linear \
  --states live record sym \
  --max-regions 1 \
  --max-boundary 250 \
  --max-interior 350 \
  --directed-frontier-cap 5 \
  --algebra-tol 1e-10 \
  --algebra-max-iter 8 \
  --gns-tol 1e-10 \
  --growth-schedule layer_batch \
  --outdir outputs/core_derived_reduced
\end{verbatim}
The schedule \code{layer\_\allowbreak{}batch} constructs all \code{GrowthStep} objects of one causal depth from the same pre-commit state before committing the births. The schedule \code{slot\_\allowbreak{}step} applies one slot closure at a time. Both schedules are implemented by \code{EmptySetGrowthModel}; the command above selects the causal-layer schedule. Other root scripts are single-surface entrypoints. They are not read in this source-surface section. A focused runner is stated only in the later section whose rows it generates.

\paragraph{Command argument meanings.}
The arguments of the integrated command select finite constructors, row emitters, and numerical caps. They do not introduce additional mathematical objects beyond the source objects listed in Table~\ref{tab:runtime-dof}.
\begin{longtable}{>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.24\linewidth}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.20\linewidth}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.48\linewidth}}
\caption{Arguments of the integrated execution command.}\label{tab:integrated-command-arguments}\\
\toprule
\textbf{Argument} & \textbf{Value in the command} & \textbf{Finite role in the generated row surface}\\
\midrule
\endfirsthead
\toprule
\textbf{Argument} & \textbf{Value in the command} & \textbf{Finite role in the generated row surface}\\
\midrule
\endhead
\code{-{}-branching} & \code{3} & arity $b$ of the finite rooted tree; each node has at most $b$ child slots and saturation is measured as occupied slots over $b$\\
\hline
\code{-{}-levels} & \code{4 5 6} & terminal depths $L$ for the finite approximants; each listed value produces a separate finite growth object and downstream response rows\\
\hline
\code{-{}-modes} & \code{linear log saturating} & selector for \code{\_mode\_scale} in the birth-weight construction; \code{rule\_coefficients} depends on \code{-{}-branching} only\\
\hline
\code{-{}-states} & \code{live record sym} & edge-layer readout: \code{record} keeps birth edges, \code{live} includes later updates, and \code{sym} reads the symmetrized edge matrix\\
\hline
\code{-{}-max-\allowbreak{}regions} & \code{1} & number of region records emitted per model before region row construction stops\\
\hline
\code{-{}-max-\allowbreak{}boundary} & \code{600} & boundary-size cap for Schur--DtN and directed-response matrices\\
\hline
\code{-{}-max-\allowbreak{}interior} & \code{900} & interior-size cap for finite elimination in Schur--DtN and directed-response calculations\\
\hline
\code{-{}-directed-\allowbreak{}frontier-\allowbreak{}cap} & \code{6} & finite frontier level used by directed-region constructors when full terminal boundaries exceed the selected cap\\
\hline
\code{-{}-algebra-\allowbreak{}tol} & \code{1e-10} & tolerance used in finite algebra closure, span projection, and residual comparisons involving algebraic bases\\
\hline
\code{-{}-algebra-\allowbreak{}max-\allowbreak{}iter} & \code{8} & iteration cap for the finite multiplication/star closure procedure in the response-algebra layer\\
\hline
\code{-{}-gns-\allowbreak{}tol} & \code{1e-10} & tolerance for support, rank, Gram-spectrum, and GNS quotient decisions\\
\hline
\code{-{}-growth-\allowbreak{}schedule} & \code{layer\_batch} & growth update route: all slots of one causal depth are evaluated from the same pre-commit state and then committed\\
\hline
\code{-{}-outdir} & \src{outputs/core_derived_documentation_run} & directory receiving the generated CSV row families for the stated command\\
\bottomrule
\end{longtable}

\subsection{Tested numerical environment and licensing}
The documented snapshot was tested under Ubuntu 26.04 LTS on Linux \code{7.0.0-27-generic} (x86\_64, glibc 2.43), using CPython 3.14.4 built with GCC 15.2.0 and NumPy 2.3.5. Explicit NumPy allocations with \code{dtype=float} resolve to \code{numpy.float64}, hence IEEE~754 binary64 arithmetic, in this environment. This arithmetic precision is distinct from the package-level constant \(\code{EPS}=10^{-12}\) and from the algebraic and GNS decision tolerances \(10^{-10}\) used by the stated command.

The numerical backend is identified by runtime mapping, dynamic-link inspection, and the configured Ubuntu package providers. NumPy links to the Ubuntu/Debian reference BLAS and LAPACK implementations, both version 3.12.1, supplied by \code{libblas3} and \code{liblapack3} package version 3.12.1-7ubuntu1. After representative matrix multiplication, linear-solve, symmetric-eigenvalue, and SVD calls, \src{/proc/self/maps} records \src{/usr/lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/blas/libblas.so.3.12.1} and \src{/usr/lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/lapack/liblapack.so.3.12.1}; \code{ldd} on the relevant NumPy extension modules resolves the same system links. \code{threadpoolctl} 3.6.0 detects no thread-pool-managed native library, consistently with the configured reference providers. The complete runtime, linker, package-provider, and NumPy build record is preserved in \src{ENVIRONMENT.txt}; a concise interpretation is given in \src{ENVIRONMENT.md}. Package versions and tolerances are fixed, but bitwise identity across other BLAS/LAPACK backends, compiler builds, or processor feature sets is not asserted.

The Python software and software documentation in the ancillary package are distributed under the MIT License in \src{LICENSE}. That software license does not set the license of this article. Distribution of the article is governed by the license selected on its arXiv record.

The documented semantic edge cases are checked by
\begin{verbatim}
cd anc/CNNA_structured_core_pkg
python3 package_consistency/check_mathematical_contracts.py
python3 package_consistency/check_finite_structure_theorems.py
python3 package_consistency/check_nested_multiscale_handoff.py
\end{verbatim}
The first check covers zero-mass normalization, normalized push-forward semantics, positive and negative GNS cyclicity controls, basis-change and nonfaithful-state quotient behavior, the support-restricted finite-\(J\) identity, and the entropy support cutoff. The second check covers finite growth replay, symmetric Schur positivity, exact finite GNS controls, sign-reversal covariance of the finite polar object, separation of backreaction observables, and prefix/carrier handoff. The third check constructs the growing first-order address-contrast carriers, verifies their exact non-unital corner embeddings and composition, checks common-ambient Schur associativity, and records the separate response, density, GNS, and finite-\(J\) naturality residuals.

\subsection{Regeneration boundary for row values}
The current growth rule changes the finite growth object before every downstream response construction. Therefore numerical statements from earlier packages, reports, CSV files, or prior runs are not inherited. Each numerical statement in later sections is written together with a command of the form displayed above, a generated row family, and a readout from rows generated by the current package. This source-surface section names commands and source routes only; it does not state numerical row values.

\subsection{Runtime degrees of freedom}
Each runtime parameter is introduced at the first object layer that uses it. Parameters are not used as labels for objects outside the layer where they first enter.

\code{-{}-branching} / $b$ & finite growth record from the empty state & arity of the finite rooted tree\\
\hline

\hline
\code{-{}-modes} / $m$ & finite birth-weight construction & selector for the implemented scalar map $\sigma_m$ used on environment load\\
\hline
\code{-{}-growth-\allowbreak{}schedule} / $\mathfrak{s}$ & finite growth record from the empty state & update schedule: \code{slot\_\allowbreak{}step} closes one slot at a time; \code{layer\_\allowbreak{}batch} evaluates one causal layer before commit\\

\hline

\bottomrule
\end{longtable}

The table is a parameter taxonomy, not a claim that every listed quantity is a physical coupling. In the reference interpretation, \(b\) is the varied structural index and \(L\) is the finite-size cutoff. The mode \(m\) selects one of three implemented birth-load maps, and \(\mathfrak{s}\) selects the update semantics; both alter the generated finite object and are therefore rule-family selectors, not derived consequences of \(b\). State labels, region counts, caps, and tolerances select readout surfaces or numerical decision procedures. Any statement that only \(b\) is varied is restricted to a command in which all other selectors are explicitly fixed.

\newpage

\section{Reference scope for discrete finite operations}
The CNNA core presented here is a discrete--finite construction. Its primitive generated objects are finite rooted address trees, finite weighted edge surfaces, finite carrier arrays, and finite matrices. The references in this document are used only to identify standard background for finite trees, finite graphs, algebraic graph operations, Schur complements, finite matrix decompositions, and finite-dimensional operator-algebraic terminology \cite{Harary1969,Bollobas1998,GodsilRoyle2001,HornJohnson2013,Zhang2005}.

These references are not external axioms for the CNNA construction. The live, record, sym, carrier, finite \(J\), and backreaction objects are generated from an empty initial configuration by the explicit finite rules implemented in the source. The branching index \(b\) enters the coefficient map, while \(L\), the mode selector \(m\), the update schedule \(\mathfrak{s}\), region selectors, caps, and numerical tolerances have separately declared roles. The cited literature documents established mathematical language in which some of these finite operations can be described. No continuum space, no integral calculus, no differential operator, and no analytic boundary-value problem is introduced in the finite core.

The term Dirichlet-to-Neumann is used here in the discrete network sense: a finite boundary response matrix obtained by eliminating interior vertices through a Schur complement. In this document, the object is entirely finite and matrix-based. Boundary sets, interior sets, invertibility checks, solve residuals, and compressed responses are computed directly from the generated finite graph data. The relevant comparison literature is finite resistor-network response theory, not a continuum field theory \cite{CurtisMorrow1991,CurtisIngermanMorrow1998}. For weighted tree graphs, Gernandt and Rohleder likewise identify the discrete Dirichlet-to-Neumann matrix with a Laplacian Schur complement and study what tree and edge-weight information can be reconstructed from it \cite{GernandtRohleder2022}. Their inverse problem starts from a symmetric positively weighted tree and a leaf boundary; the present construction instead generates directed record/live weights and uses the Schur map in the forward provenance chain. The citation therefore supplies a close tree--DtN comparator, not an identity of problems or conclusions.

\section{Derivation graph}
\subsection{Global object order}
The documentation follows the first-use order of the objects. When one Python module contributes to several object layers, only the function block whose inputs are already available is introduced at that point.
\begin{center}

Derived row modules do not introduce primitive degrees of freedom. They attach finite measurements to objects constructed earlier in the chain.

\newpage
\section{Core construction initialized by the empty configuration}
\subsection{Finite arithmetic layer}
\paragraph{Code map.} The module \code{core/math\_\allowbreak{}utils.py} defines finite numerical primitives: Frobenius norm, total variation distance, probability normalization, and row-metric extraction. These are not CNNA axioms; they are deterministic finite arithmetic functions used by all later measurements.

\begin{definition}[Finite probability normalization]
For a finite vector or dictionary, the implementation first replaces every negative entry, and for array inputs every non-finite entry, by zero. Writing the resulting values as \(x_i^+\) and \(s=\sum_i x_i^+\), the implemented normalization is
\[
  \mathcal N_{\varepsilon}(x)=
  \begin{cases}
    (x_i^+/s)_i, & s>\varepsilon,\\[0.4em]
    (1/n,\ldots,1/n), & s\le\varepsilon\text{ and }n>0,\\[0.4em]
    (), & n=0.
  \end{cases}
\]
For a non-empty zero-mass input the fallback is therefore the uniform distribution, not a zero-mass object. Dictionary normalization applies the same non-negative clipping; its keys are retained.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Total variation is a finite seminorm]
For two finite probability vectors \(p,q\), the implemented quantity
\[
  \operatorname{TV}(p,q)=\frac12\sum_i |p_i-q_i|
\]
vanishes when \(p=q\) and is non-negative.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
\textbf{Object.} The object is the pair of finite arrays used by \code{tv\_\allowbreak{}arr} or dictionaries used by \code{tv}. \textbf{Proof.} Each summand \(|p_i-q_i|\) is non-negative; hence the sum and one-half multiple are non-negative. If \(p=q\), each summand is zero. \textbf{Counter-check.} The converse requires the index supports to be compared after the common-key completion used by the dictionary implementation. \textbf{Conclusion.} The quantity is an exact finite discrepancy measure, not a fitted parameter.
\end{proof}



\subsection{Empty-set growth object}
\paragraph{Code map.} The module \code{core/emptyset\_\allowbreak{}growth.py} contains \code{RuleCoefficients}, \code{Node}, \code{Event}, \code{OpenBirthSlot}, \code{GrowthStep}, and \code{EmptySetGrowthModel}. The constructor records \code{empty\_\allowbreak{}state}, creates the root by \code{birth\_\allowbreak{}root\_\allowbreak{}from\_\allowbreak{}empty}, and then processes finite open child slots. The source separates causal depth, sibling slot rank, technical linearization index, and update schedule. It does not treat the total event-list order as the source temporal object.

\begin{definition}[Finite CNNA growth approximant with schedule]
For branching arity \(b\ge 2\), level \(L\ge 0\), mode \(m\in\{\mathrm{linear},\mathrm{log},\mathrm{saturating}\}\), and growth schedule \(\mathfrak{s}\in\{\mathrm{slot\_step},\mathrm{layer\_batch}\}\), the finite approximant is
\begin{equation}
  G_{b,L,m,\mathfrak{s}}=(V,\mathcal E,E_{\mathrm{record}},E_{\mathrm{live}},a,\ell,p,d,\tau,r,\lambda,g,g_{\mathrm{birth}},q).
  \label{eq:finite-growth-approximant}
\end{equation}
Here \(V\) is the finite node list; \(a(v)\) is the finite address; \(\ell(v)\) is the address level; \(p(v)\) is the parent except for the root; \(d(v)\) is the recorded causal depth; \(\tau(v)\) is the event-list index of the selected finite execution; \(r(v)\) is the sibling slot rank; \(\lambda(v)\) is the linearization index inside the schedule; \(g(v)\) is the current node load; \(g_{\mathrm{birth}}(v)\) is the load at the birth update; and \(q(v)\) is the recorded response weight \code{lapse\_\allowbreak{}weight}. The edge dictionaries \(E_{\mathrm{record}}\) and \(E_{\mathrm{live}}\) are finite directed weighted dictionaries.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Initial boundary event]
The transition from the empty state to the root is recorded as \code{birth\_\allowbreak{}root\_\allowbreak{}from\_\allowbreak{}empty}. It is the finite initial boundary event of the implemented construction. It is not derived from a prior response matrix, because before the root there is no finite parent, boundary, sibling set, or conductance environment in the source tree.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Open birth slot, saturation, and finite growth step]
For a parent node \(p\), \code{open\_\allowbreak{}birth\_\allowbreak{}slots} returns one \code{OpenBirthSlot} for each unoccupied rank \(r\in\{0,\ldots,b-1\}\). A parent is saturated exactly when its \code{child\_\allowbreak{}by\_\allowbreak{}rank} dictionary has cardinality \(b\). A \code{GrowthStep} closes one such slot and records the slot, causal predecessors, occupied sibling slots before the update, environment load, birth weight, response weight, and linearization index.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Growth schedules]
The schedule \code{slot\_\allowbreak{}step} linearizes open slots and applies one \code{GrowthStep} immediately. The schedule \code{layer\_\allowbreak{}batch} first constructs all \code{GrowthStep} objects for the open slots of one causal depth from the same pre-commit state, then commits the births, and then adds sibling relations by slot rank. Thus \code{layer\_\allowbreak{}batch} removes slot-sibling update order inside a causal layer; it retains parent-before-child causal order and slot-rank structure.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Symmetric environment load of an open slot]
For a parent node \(p\) and the occupied sibling set \(U_p\) read from \code{child\_\allowbreak{}by\_\allowbreak{}rank}, the function \code{\_birth\_\allowbreak{}environment\_\allowbreak{}load} computes the finite scalar
\begin{equation}
  h(p,U_p)=g(p)+\sum_{a\in \mathrm{Anc}(p)}\frac{g(a)}{(\mathrm{depth}(a,p)+1)^2}
  +\begin{cases}
    \dfrac{\sum_{s\in U_p} g(s)}{|U_p|+1}, & U_p\ne\varnothing,\\[0.4em]
    0, & U_p=\varnothing .
  \end{cases}
  \label{eq:birth-environment-load}
\end{equation}
The sibling contribution is a set sum over occupied sibling nodes. It has no factor depending on the enumeration position of a sibling in a previous birth sequence.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Branching-derived rule coefficients]
The function \code{rule\_coefficients} maps the arity $b$ to the tuple $c_b$ with fields and values
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  c_b.\code{env\_birth\_edge\_bias} &= \frac{1}{(b+1)^2}, &
  c_b.\code{forward\_rank\_bias} &= \frac{1}{b+3},\\
  c_b.\code{backward\_base} &= \frac12+\frac{1}{2(b+2)}, &
  c_b.\code{backward\_rank\_bias} &= \frac{1}{(b+1)(b+3)},\\
  c_b.\code{ancestor\_backreaction} &= \frac{1}{b(b+1)}, &
  c_b.\code{ancestor\_node\_load} &= \frac{1}{(b+2)^2},\\
  c_b.\code{sibling\_backreaction} &= \frac{1}{b(b+2)}, &
  c_b.\code{sibling\_forward\_asym} &= 1+\frac{1}{b+1},\\
  c_b.\code{sibling\_backward\_asym} &= 1-\frac{1}{b+1}, &
  c_b.\code{sibling\_node\_load} &= \frac{1}{(b+7)^2},\\
  c_b.\code{child\_env\_load} &= \frac{1}{(b+7)^2}.&&
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:branching-rule-coefficients}
\end{equation}
The tuple in Equation~\eqref{eq:branching-rule-coefficients} is evaluated from the single integer $b$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Mode-scale map and birth weight]
The function \code{\_mode\_scale} applies one of the three finite scalar maps
\begin{equation}
  \sigma_m(x)=
  \begin{cases}
    x, & m=\code{linear},\\
    \log(1+\max(0,x)), & m=\code{log},\\
    \dfrac{x}{1+|x|}, & m=\code{saturating}.
  \end{cases}
  \label{eq:mode-scale-map}
\end{equation}
For a slot of parent $p$, the corresponding \code{GrowthStep} stores
\begin{equation}
  g_{\rm birth}=1+\frac{\sigma_m(h(p,U_p))}{1+\ell(p)+b}.
  \label{eq:birth-weight}
\end{equation}
The same value is copied to \code{lapse\_weight}. The current load of the new child is then incremented by the separate child-environment update recorded in \code{child\_env\_load}.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Base birth-edge weights]
For sibling rank $r\in\{0,\ldots,b-1\}$ let $\rho_r=(r+1)/b$ and
\begin{equation}
  w_0 = 1+c_b.\code{env\_birth\_edge\_bias}\;\sigma_m(h(p,U_p)).
  \label{eq:base-birth-edge-weight}
\end{equation}
The directed parent-child weights inserted at birth are
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  w_{p\to v} &= w_0\bigl(1+c_b.\code{forward\_rank\_bias}\;\rho_r\bigr),\\
  w_{v\to p} &= w_0\bigl(c_b.\code{backward\_base}+c_b.\code{backward\_rank\_bias}\;\rho_r\bigr).
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:directed-birth-edge-weights}
\end{equation}
These two directed weights are inserted into both the record and live edge dictionaries.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Node count of the complete finite approximant]
For \(G_{b,L,m,\mathfrak{s}}\) constructed by \code{EmptySetGrowthModel},
\begin{equation}
  |V|=\sum_{k=0}^L b^k.
  \label{eq:complete-approximant-node-count}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
\textbf{Object.} The object is the list \code{self.nodes}. \textbf{Step 1.} The constructor creates exactly one root node at level \(0\). \textbf{Step 2.} For every node at depth \(k<L\), \code{open\_\allowbreak{}birth\_\allowbreak{}slots} contains exactly the unoccupied ranks of that parent. \textbf{Step 3.} The schedules differ in commit order, but both close every open slot of the processed depth exactly once. \textbf{Step 4.} A closed slot of a level \(k\) parent creates one child at level \(k+1\). By induction, level \(k\) contains \(b^k\) addresses. \textbf{Counter-check.} The method \code{node\_\allowbreak{}count\_\allowbreak{}expected} implements the same finite sum. A mismatch is a construction mismatch for the selected schedule, not a continuum statement. \textbf{Conclusion.} The count is an exact finite identity of the generated approximant.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Causal depth is separated from linearization index]
For non-root nodes, \(d(v)=d(p(v))+1\) is the causal-depth relation recorded by the slot. The quantity \(\lambda(v)\) is the finite ordering index of the selected schedule and is not the parent-before-child relation.
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
\textbf{Object.} The object is the pair \code{OpenBirthSlot} and \code{GrowthStep}. \textbf{Step 1.} An open slot stores \code{causal\_\allowbreak{}depth = parent.level + 1}. \textbf{Step 2.} \code{\_linearize\_\allowbreak{}open\_\allowbreak{}slots} sorts slots by \code{rank} or \code{reverse\_\allowbreak{}rank} after causal depth and parent fields. \textbf{Step 3.} \code{GrowthStep.linearization\_\allowbreak{}index} records this schedule index. \textbf{Counter-check.} The derived row family \code{birth\_\allowbreak{}linearization\_\allowbreak{}invariance\_\allowbreak{}rows} compares \code{rank} and \code{reverse\_\allowbreak{}rank} by address-level residuals. In this package the \code{layer\_\allowbreak{}batch} route is the linearization-insensitive route for that comparison, while \code{slot\_\allowbreak{}step} records finite schedule dependence. \textbf{Conclusion.} The source separates causal order from slot linearization.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Layer-batch removes sampled slot-linearization dependence at address level]
For the implemented comparison \(\eta=\mathrm{rank}\) against \(\eta=\mathrm{reverse\_rank}\), the \code{layer\_\allowbreak{}batch} route gives identical address-indexed node fields and edge dictionaries up to the reported numerical tolerance. The \code{slot\_\allowbreak{}step} route need not do so.
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
\textbf{Object.} The objects are \code{OpenBirthSlot}, \code{GrowthStep}, and the edge dictionaries indexed back to node addresses. \textbf{Step 1.} In \code{layer\_\allowbreak{}batch}, the list of \code{GrowthStep} records is built before the corresponding children are committed. Therefore each step reads the same pre-commit occupied sibling set for its parent. \textbf{Step 2.} The environment load uses the symmetric set expression \(\sum_{s\in U_p}g(s)/(|U_p|+1)\), so it does not depend on an order of the occupied siblings. \textbf{Step 3.} The birth weights are stored inside the \code{GrowthStep} record and are then used by \code{\_apply\_\allowbreak{}growth\_\allowbreak{}step}. \textbf{Step 4.} Batch sibling relations are added after commit by grouping children by parent and sorting by \code{sibling\_\allowbreak{}rank}; the relation is a slot-rank relation, not a commit-order relation. \textbf{Counter-check.} The package exposes the \code{rank}/\code{reverse\_\allowbreak{}rank} comparison, not a full permutation harness. The \code{slot\_\allowbreak{}step} route can have non-zero residuals because each slot is applied before the next one is evaluated. \textbf{Conclusion.} The causal-layer schedule separates the finite parent-before-child relation from the sampled ordering of slots inside one causal depth.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Record-live separation]
At birth, a parent-child directed pair is inserted into both \(E_{\mathrm{record}}\) and \(E_{\mathrm{live}}\). Later ancestor and slot-sibling updates are inserted only into \(E_{\mathrm{live}}\) and node loads, not into \(E_{\mathrm{record}}\).
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
\textbf{Object.} The objects are the dictionaries \code{record\_\allowbreak{}edges} and \code{live\_\allowbreak{}edges}. \textbf{Step 1.} The birth edge weights \(w_{\rightarrow}\) and \(w_{\leftarrow}\) are computed from the \code{GrowthStep} record and inserted into both dictionaries in \code{\_apply\_\allowbreak{}growth\_\allowbreak{}step}. \textbf{Step 2.} Ancestor updates and sibling-slot relation updates call \code{add\_\allowbreak{}edge} only on \code{live\_\allowbreak{}edges}. \textbf{Step 3.} Under \code{layer\_\allowbreak{}batch}, the live updates of a causal layer use the \code{GrowthStep} fields evaluated from the frozen pre-commit state; record edges still store only the parent-child birth relation. \textbf{Step 4.} The same update changes current node loads \(g\), while \(g_{\mathrm{birth}}\) remains the value recorded at the birth update. \textbf{Counter-check.} \code{slot\_\allowbreak{}step} and \code{layer\_\allowbreak{}batch} can produce different live layers because \code{slot\_\allowbreak{}step} evaluates later slots after earlier commits. Record rows are closer to schedule-independent structure because they omit ancestor and slot-sibling live updates, but their numerical weights still come from the selected schedule. \textbf{Conclusion.} The code realizes two distinct finite layers: birth record and current live state.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The sym edge layer is a readout, not a schedule]
The state selector \code{sym} is implemented by symmetrizing the adjacency read from \code{live\_\allowbreak{}edges}. It cancels directed skew information at readout level. It is not a separate growth schedule and it does not imply that \code{slot\_\allowbreak{}step} and \code{layer\_\allowbreak{}batch} have identical edge weights. The finite comparison represented in \code{birth\_\allowbreak{}linearization\_\allowbreak{}invariance\_\allowbreak{}rows} compares \code{rank} against \code{reverse\_\allowbreak{}rank} inside a selected schedule.
\end{remark}

\paragraph{Row-generation command: causal-layer route.}
{\scriptsize
\begin{verbatim}
cd anc/CNNA_structured_core_pkg
PYTHONPATH=src python3 run_cnna.py \
  --branching 3 \
  --levels 2 3 4 \
  --modes linear log saturating \
  --states live record sym \
  --max-regions 1 \
  --max-boundary 250 \
  --max-interior 350 \
  --directed-frontier-cap 5 \
  --algebra-tol 1e-10 \
  --algebra-max-iter 8 \
  --gns-tol 1e-10 \
  --growth-schedule layer_batch \
  --outdir outputs/growth_carrier_f1f2_layer_batch
\end{verbatim}
}

\paragraph{Comparison command: slot-step route.}
{\scriptsize
\begin{verbatim}
cd anc/CNNA_structured_core_pkg
PYTHONPATH=src python3 run_cnna.py \
  --branching 3 \
  --levels 2 3 4 \
  --modes linear log saturating \
  --states live record sym \
  --max-regions 1 \
  --max-boundary 250 \
  --max-interior 350 \
  --directed-frontier-cap 5 \
  --algebra-tol 1e-10 \
  --algebra-max-iter 8 \
  --gns-tol 1e-10 \
  --growth-schedule slot_step \
  --outdir outputs/growth_carrier_f1f2_slot_step_comparison
\end{verbatim}
}

\subsection{Birth-relative complement meaning of CNNA}\label{sec:birth-relative-complement}
\paragraph{Terminology and code map.}
The name CNNA is used here for a \emph{ComplemeNt Net Architecture}. The word complement refers first to the finite carrier enlargement implemented by \code{EmptySetGrowthModel}; the word network refers to the directed couplings inserted when that enlargement is committed. These are two distinct steps and should not be conflated.

\begin{definition}[Birth-relative vertex complement]
Let $e$ be an accepted non-root birth event and let $v_e$ be its new node. Write $V_e^-$ for the vertex set immediately before \code{\_apply\_growth\_step} commits $v_e$, and $V_e^+$ for the vertex set immediately afterward. Then
\begin{equation}
  V_e^+=V_e^-\,\dot\cup\,\{v_e\},
  \qquad
  \{v_e\}=V_e^+\setminus V_e^-,
  \qquad
  V_e^-=V_e^+\setminus\{v_e\}.
  \label{eq:birth-relative-set-complement}
\end{equation}
The dot denotes disjoint union. The statement is relative to this finite update; it does not presuppose a fixed infinite universal carrier. The root event is the base case $V_0^-=\varnothing$, $V_0^+=\{r\}$; it creates the first coordinate but has no prior network to which it could be coupled.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Coordinate complement]
For a finite vertex set $V$, let $\R^V$ denote the real coordinate space with standard basis $(\delta_v)_{v\in V}$. Zero extension along the inclusion $V_e^-\hookrightarrow V_e^+$ gives an injective map
\begin{equation}
  \iota_e:\R^{V_e^-}\longrightarrow\R^{V_e^+},
  \qquad
  (\iota_e x)(u)=
  \begin{cases}
    x(u), & u\in V_e^-,\\
    0, & u=v_e.
  \end{cases}
  \label{eq:birth-zero-extension}
\end{equation}
The post-birth carrier has the exact direct-sum decomposition
\begin{equation}
  \R^{V_e^+}
  =\iota_e(\R^{V_e^-})\oplus\operatorname{span}_{\R}\{\delta_{v_e}\}.
  \label{eq:birth-relative-coordinate-complement}
\end{equation}
Thus the newborn node contributes one new real coordinate direction complementary to the embedded pre-birth carrier.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Exactness and schedule scope of the complement step]
Equation~\eqref{eq:birth-relative-coordinate-complement} is exact for every committed node. For \code{slot\_step} it is also the primitive update decomposition. For \code{layer\_batch}, let $N_d$ be the nodes born at causal depth $d$ from one frozen pre-commit state $V_d^-$. The schedule-invariant causal statement is the batch decomposition
\begin{equation}
  V_d^+=V_d^-\,\dot\cup\,N_d,
  \qquad
  \R^{V_d^+}
  =\iota_d(\R^{V_d^-})\oplus
    \operatorname{span}_{\R}\{\delta_v:v\in N_d\}.
  \label{eq:layer-batch-coordinate-complement}
\end{equation}
The nodewise decompositions inside that batch remain exact, but their internal commit order is a technical linearization and is not promoted to an additional causal order.
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
\textbf{Object.} The objects are the address dictionary \code{addr\_to\_id}, the node list \code{nodes}, and the selected \code{GrowthStep} records. \textbf{Step 1.} Before committing a step, the source rejects any address already present in \code{addr\_to\_id}. Hence the new address is not in $V^-$. \textbf{Step 2.} The source appends exactly one node and enters exactly one new address, which proves Equation~\eqref{eq:birth-relative-set-complement}. \textbf{Step 3.} Every vector on $V^+$ splits uniquely into its restriction to $V^-$ and its coefficient at the new standard basis vector; this proves Equation~\eqref{eq:birth-relative-coordinate-complement}. \textbf{Step 4.} Under \code{layer\_batch}, all \code{GrowthStep} records of one depth are constructed before any of their nodes is committed. Distinct open slots have distinct addresses, so the same argument applied to the complete newborn set gives Equation~\eqref{eq:layer-batch-coordinate-complement}. \textbf{Counter-check.} The direct sum is a statement about the standard address-coordinate carrier. It is not yet a statement about orthogonality in a later response metric, GNS metric, or state-dependent inner product. \textbf{Conclusion.} The complement step is a finite exact carrier identity with an explicit schedule scope.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Directed coupling of the complement]
Order the coordinates of one update as old vertices followed by the newborn set $N$. The record and live adjacency matrices have finite block forms
\begin{equation}
  W_{\rm record}^{+}
  =
  \begin{pmatrix}
    W_{\rm record}^{-} & C_{\rm parent}\\
    D_{\rm parent} & 0
  \end{pmatrix},
  \qquad
  W_{\rm live}^{+}
  =
  \begin{pmatrix}
    W_{\rm live}^{-} & C_{\rm live}\\
    D_{\rm live} & W_{NN}
  \end{pmatrix}.
  \label{eq:complement-coupling-blocks}
\end{equation}
Here $C_{\rm parent}$ and $D_{\rm parent}$ contain the two directed parent--child birth weights of Equation~\eqref{eq:directed-birth-edge-weights}. The live off-diagonal blocks additionally contain the implemented ancestor and sibling couplings, while $W_{NN}$ contains the slot-rank sibling relations among nodes born in the same layer. In a one-node \code{slot\_step} update, $W_{NN}=0$. Because the forward and backward coefficients are generally unequal, neither block matrix is required to be symmetric.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[The complement is coupled rather than independent]
The carrier identity in Equation~\eqref{eq:birth-relative-coordinate-complement} does not make the newborn line dynamically independent of the old carrier. For every non-root birth, both parent--child entries in the record and live dictionaries are non-zero and are generated from the same finite growth step. The live layer can add further directed couplings to causal predecessors and sibling slots and can update existing node loads.
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
\textbf{Object.} The objects are \code{record\_edges}, \code{live\_edges}, and the node-load field $g$. \textbf{Step 1.} Equation~\eqref{eq:directed-birth-edge-weights} gives positive parent-to-child and child-to-parent weights for every admitted $b$, mode, and finite environment load generated by the source. \textbf{Step 2.} \code{\_apply\_growth\_step} inserts both weights into both edge dictionaries. \textbf{Step 3.} The ancestor loop inserts additional child-to-predecessor live entries and changes predecessor loads. \textbf{Step 4.} The sibling routines insert unequal forward/backward live entries according to slot rank. \textbf{Counter-check.} The set/direct-sum complement would remain true even if all cross-couplings were zero. Hence complementarity alone does not prove network interaction. \textbf{Conclusion.} CNNA combines an exact carrier complement with a separate generated coupling rule.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[What complement does not mean]
The term does not denote the graph complement, a Boolean complement, an orthogonal complement with respect to a derived matrix $S$, a commutant of an operator algebra, or a claim that the newborn degree of freedom is statistically independent. Relative to the terminal carrier one also has the tautology $V_L=(V_L\setminus\{v\})\dot\cup\{v\}$ for every vertex, but that terminal identity discards the birth provenance and is not the definition used here. Such stronger structures occur, if at all, only after additional definitions and tests. The primitive complement claims are the birth- and layer-relative Equations~\eqref{eq:birth-relative-set-complement}, \eqref{eq:birth-relative-coordinate-complement}, and \eqref{eq:layer-batch-coordinate-complement}.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Complement-to-response bridge and its non-implication]
Choose a finite selected set $B\dot\cup I$ after the directed complement couplings have been generated. Form the directed local matrix $K^{\rm dir}$ from the ordered weights and, when the interior solve is accepted, define
\begin{equation}
  K^{\rm dir}_{II}X=K^{\rm dir}_{IB},
  \qquad
  \Lambda_B^{\rm dir}=K^{\rm dir}_{BB}-K^{\rm dir}_{BI}X,
  \qquad
  \Lambda_B^{\rm dir}=S_B+A_B,
  \label{eq:complement-to-directed-response}
\end{equation}
with $S_B^T=S_B$ and $A_B^T=-A_B$ as in Equation~\eqref{eq:symmetric-skew-response-split}. The carrier-complement identities do not imply $A_B\ne0$. A non-zero skew response requires both asymmetric generated coupling data and survival of that asymmetry under the selected boundary/interior elimination and compression.
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
\textbf{Object.} The objects are the directed edge matrix, its local response matrix, and the accepted Schur response. \textbf{Step 1.} Equations~\eqref{eq:birth-relative-coordinate-complement} and \eqref{eq:layer-batch-coordinate-complement} only enlarge the coordinate domain. \textbf{Step 2.} Equation~\eqref{eq:complement-coupling-blocks} supplies the ordered couplings from which $K^{\rm dir}$ is built. \textbf{Step 3.} The Schur operation eliminates $I$ and returns a boundary matrix. \textbf{Step 4.} Every real square matrix has the exact symmetric/skew split. \textbf{Counter-check.} If the generated weights are replaced by a symmetric control, then the local Laplacian and its accepted Schur complement are symmetric and $A_B=0$ up to numerical residual. Conversely, a non-symmetric local matrix can still yield zero skew part on a particular compressed boundary. \textbf{Conclusion.} The logical chain is complement enlargement, directed coupling, Schur reduction, and only then symmetric/skew decomposition; none of these arrows may be reversed without an additional theorem.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Carrier and prefix projections}
\paragraph{Code map.} The module \code{core/projective\_\allowbreak{}maps.py} defines address truncation \code{prefix}, terminal carrier extraction, terminal state extraction, push-forward maps, center subsets, and response-energy distributions.

\begin{definition}[Normalized prefix push-forward]
Let \(\Omega_L\) be the terminal address set at level \(L\). For \(0\le k\le L\), define \(\pi_k:\Omega_L\to\Omega_k\) by address truncation and let the raw fiber sum be
\begin{equation}
  (\pi_{k\,*}^{\rm raw}\mu)(u)=\sum_{\omega:\pi_k(\omega)=u}\mu(\omega).
  \label{eq:terminal-prefix-pushforward}
\end{equation}
The function \code{push\_\allowbreak{}forward} returns \(\mathcal N_{\varepsilon}(\pi_{k\,*}^{\rm raw}\mu)\). Thus it agrees with the ordinary push-forward for an already normalized non-negative input, but it renormalizes a general finite input and applies the uniform fallback when the raw output has no positive mass.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Terminal carrier and terminal diagonal state]
The terminal carrier is the uniform finite distribution on \(\Omega_L\). For a terminal node \(v\), let \(I_{\rm abs}(v)\) be the sum of absolute weights of all selected directed edges incident to \(v\), counting incoming and outgoing incidences exactly as in the edge dictionary. The unnormalized terminal-state weight is
\[
  d_s(v)=\max\!\left(\varepsilon,\,g(v)+0.05\,I_{\rm abs}(v)\right),
\]
and the terminal diagonal state is \(\mathcal N_{\varepsilon}(d_s)\). The \code{record} state reads \code{record\_edges}; \code{live} and \code{sym} use the same positive proxy from \code{live\_edges}. Consequently the terminal positive proxy does not distinguish live from sym, although their directed response readouts do. Signed current is never inserted into this positive carrier.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Probability preservation for normalized inputs]
If \(\mu\) is a finite non-negative probability distribution, then \code{push\_\allowbreak{}forward} returns the ordinary prefix push-forward and its total mass is one.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
\textbf{Object.} The object is the dictionary passed to \code{push\_\allowbreak{}forward}. \textbf{Step 1.} Every terminal key has exactly one truncated prefix. \textbf{Step 2.} The raw fiber sum in Equation~\eqref{eq:terminal-prefix-pushforward} partitions the source support and therefore has total mass one. \textbf{Step 3.} Applying \(\mathcal N_{\varepsilon}\) to a non-negative mass-one dictionary leaves it unchanged. \textbf{Counter-check.} For a non-normalized input, the implementation returns the normalized raw push-forward rather than preserving the original total mass. \textbf{Conclusion.} Exact projectivity statements apply to the normalized probability inputs used by the carrier rows.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Generated row families.}

\subsection{Whole-network F1/F2 axes and signed current scalar}
The historical row label \code{F2\_birth\_order} denotes the canonical sibling-slot rank encoded in node addresses. It is not the execution order of the event list; under \code{layer\_batch}, births at one causal depth are evaluated from the same pre-commit state.

\paragraph{Code map.} The module \code{core/signed\_\allowbreak{}current.py} constructs an orthonormal F1/F2 pair and an orientation measurement from finite node-address data and a selected edge dictionary. This whole-network current is introduced before Schur--DtN response; it does not require a selected boundary/interior cut.

\begin{definition}[Whole-network F1/F2 plane]
The function \code{F1\_F2\_vectors} assigns to a node $v$ with address $a(v)=(r_1,\ldots,r_{\ell(v)})$ the finite coordinates
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  F_1(v)&=\begin{cases}
    \ell(v)/L, & L>0,\\
    0, & L=0,
  \end{cases}
  &
  F_2(v)&=\sum_{d=1}^{\ell(v)}\frac{1}{d}
  \frac{r_d-(b-1)/2}{\max(1,(b-1)/2)}.
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:whole-network-f1-f2-fields}
\end{equation}
For the root the sum is empty and hence zero. The function \code{orthonormal\_pair} mean-centers and Gram-Schmidt orthonormalizes these two vectors when the finite rank is above the implemented fallback threshold.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Whole-network signed-current scalar]
For a selected edge layer, \code{orientation\_\allowbreak{}measurement} computes the directed norm, symmetric norm, skew norm, relative skew norm, and the scalar circulation in the F1/F2 plane. For \code{state=sym}, the skew part is set to zero at readout level.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[F1/F2 current is independent of Schur reduction]
The whole-network F1/F2 scalar is computed from the finite edge dictionary and node-address vectors before any Schur boundary/interior split is chosen.
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
\textbf{Object.} The object is the output of \code{orientation\_\allowbreak{}measurement}. \textbf{Step 1.} \code{F1\_\allowbreak{}F2\_\allowbreak{}vectors} reads only node levels and address ranks. \textbf{Step 2.} \code{orientation\_\allowbreak{}measurement} reads \code{record\_\allowbreak{}edges} for \code{record}, \code{live\_\allowbreak{}edges} for \code{live}, and the symmetrized readout for \code{sym}. \textbf{Step 3.} No boundary list, interior list, Schur solve, or response compression is called. \textbf{Counter-check.} Regional F1/F2 role bases in later directed-response sections are different objects; they are not this whole-network scalar. \textbf{Conclusion.} The F1/F2 current is a finite whole-network measurement attached to the growth and carrier layer.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Symmetric Schur--DtN response on a selected finite cut}
\paragraph{Code map.} The module \code{core/schur\_\allowbreak{}dtn.py} defines \code{SchurResponse}, \code{RegionSpec}, \code{schur\_\allowbreak{}response}, \code{schur\_\allowbreak{}response\_\allowbreak{}from\_\allowbreak{}model}, sibling-region construction, boundary role bases, response compression, and atom keys. The selected finite cut enters here for the first time: a boundary list \(B\), an interior list \(I\), and a finite local matrix \(K\) are passed to the Schur reduction.

\begin{definition}[Finite Schur--DtN response]
Given a finite symmetric local matrix \(K\) and a disjoint boundary/interior split \(B\sqcup I\), the finite response matrix is
\begin{equation}
  \Lambda_B = K_{BB}-K_{BI}X,\qquad K_{II}X=K_{IB}.
  \label{eq:finite-schur-dtn-response}
\end{equation}
when the interior block \(K_{II}\) satisfies the condition-number guard. The source uses \code{np.linalg.solve}; it does not form an explicit matrix inverse.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Accepted Schur response records a finite linear solve]
If \code{schur\_\allowbreak{}response} returns \code{ok=True}, then the returned object contains the Schur matrix, the condition number of \(K_{II}\), the solve residual \(\|K_{II}X-K_{IB}\|_F/\max(\|K_{IB}\|_F,\varepsilon)\), and the row-sum residual of \(\Lambda_B\).
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
\textbf{Object.} The object is \code{SchurResponse}. \textbf{Step 1.} The function rejects empty boundary lists, boundary/interior overlap, and interior blocks above the condition guard. \textbf{Step 2.} It solves \(K_{II}X=K_{IB}\). \textbf{Step 3.} It returns the response in Equation~\eqref{eq:finite-schur-dtn-response}, symmetrized as \((\Lambda_B+\Lambda_B^T)/2\). In \code{schur\_\allowbreak{}response\_\allowbreak{}from\_\allowbreak{}model}, diagonal degrees include conductance from selected nodes to the full current network, while off-diagonal entries are retained only between selected nodes. Omitted external neighbors therefore remain as grounded diagonal load. \textbf{Counter-check.} The resulting open-grounded response need not satisfy \(\Lambda_B\mathbf 1=0\); the row-sum residual measures this finite leakage. Non-accepted branches return an error string and no response matrix. \textbf{Conclusion.} The accepted row is a finite open-grounded Schur reduction with recorded numerical guards, not necessarily a conservative response of an isolated selected subgraph.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Execution command.} The following command generated the row families read in this subsection and the two following subsections. It uses the current growth rule and the causal-layer schedule.
\begin{verbatim}
cd anc/CNNA_structured_core_pkg
PYTHONPATH=src python3 run_cnna.py \
  --branching 3 \
  --levels 4 \
  --modes linear log saturating \
  --states live record sym \
  --max-regions 2 \
  --max-boundary 600 \
  --max-interior 900 \
  --directed-frontier-cap 6 \
  --algebra-tol 1e-10 \
  --algebra-max-iter 8 \
  --gns-tol 1e-10 \
  --growth-schedule layer_batch \
  --outdir outputs/schur_directed_j_layer_batch_reduced
\end{verbatim}
